Без устранения этих уязвимостей система не может считаться безопасной и готовой к production-развертыванию. Для military-grade реализации необходимо:

1. Переписать алгоритм восстановления секрета с использованием более надежного алгоритма, чем Бабай
2. Реализовать NTT с гарантированно постоянным временем выполнения
3. Добавить механизм проверки накопленной ошибки по всей цепочке
4. Реализовать криптографически надежную проверку доступности данных
5. Обеспечить полную изоляцию между префиксами
6. Использовать более надежное преобразование хеша в скаляр
7. Предоставить строгое доказательство эквивалентности CVP и SVP для k=4

Без этих исправлений система остается уязвимой к скрытым атакам, которые могут проявиться только через длительный период времени, делая систему ненадежной без возможности обнаружения до катастрофического отказа.

---



# КОРРЕКТНАЯ И БЕЗОПАСНАЯ РЕАЛИЗАЦИЯ РЕКУРСИВНЫХ ДОКАЗАТЕЛЬСТВ

## 1. Исправление восстановления секрета при адаптивном выборе ошибок

```rust
// src/crypto/proofs.rs

/// Babai's nearest plane algorithm with enhanced security for CVP
fn solve_for_y(
    v: &Vector,
    c1: i64,
    c2: i64,
    params: &VerifiedRingLweParams,
) -> Result<(Vector, Vector), &'static str> {
    // Step 1: Generate the lattice basis
    let basis = Self::generate_lattice_basis(c1, c2, params);
  
    // Step 2: Apply BKZ reduction (more secure than LLL for high dimensions)
    let reduced_basis = Self::bkz_reduction(&basis, params, 0.99)?;
  
    // Step 3: Apply Babai's nearest plane algorithm with multiple rounds
    let target = Self::vector_to_lattice_point(v, params);
    let solutions = Self::babai_multiple_rounds(&reduced_basis, &target, params, 3)?;
  
    // Step 4: Verify all candidate solutions
    let mut valid_solutions = Vec::new();
    for solution in solutions {
        let (y1, y2) = Self::lattice_point_to_vectors(&solution, params)?;
      
        // Verify the solution
        let lhs = y1.mul(c2).sub(&y2.mul(c1));
        let diff = lhs.sub(v);
      
        // Check if the difference is within acceptable bounds
        if diff.norm_infty() <= 2 && y1.is_very_small() && y2.is_very_small() {
            valid_solutions.push((y1, y2, diff.norm_infty()));
        }
    }
  
    // Step 5: Select the best solution (with smallest error)
    if let Some((y1, y2, _)) = valid_solutions.into_iter().min_by_key(|(_, _, error)| *error) {
        Ok((y1, y2))
    } else {
        Err("No valid solution found for CVP")
    }
}

/// BKZ lattice basis reduction algorithm (more secure than LLL for high dimensions)
fn bkz_reduction(basis: &Matrix, params: &VerifiedRingLweParams, delta: f64) -> Result<Matrix, &'static str> {
    // BKZ (Block Korkine-Zolotarev) reduction is more secure than LLL for high dimensions
    // It guarantees a better approximation factor for the shortest vector problem
  
    let mut reduced = basis.clone();
    let n = reduced.rows();
  
    // BKZ reduction with block size β = 20 (standard value for security)
    let block_size = 20;
  
    // Main BKZ loop
    let mut k = 1;
    while k < n {
        // Size reduction
        for j in (0..k).rev() {
            let mu_kj = reduced.get_mu(k, j);
            if mu_kj.abs() > 0.5 {
                let r = mu_kj.round();
                // Reduce vector k
                reduced.size_reduce(k, j, r);
            }
        }
      
        // Local SVP reduction in the block
        if k >= block_size - 1 {
            Self::local_svp_reduction(&mut reduced, k - block_size + 1, block_size, params)?;
        }
      
        // Lovász condition
        if !Self::lovasz_condition(&reduced, k, delta) {
            // Swap vectors k and k-1
            reduced.swap_rows(k, k-1);
            k = k.saturating_sub(1);
        } else {
            k += 1;
        }
    }
  
    Ok(reduced)
}

/// Local SVP reduction for BKZ
fn local_svp_reduction(matrix: &mut Matrix, start: usize, block_size: usize, params: &VerifiedRingLweParams) -> Result<(), &'static str> {
    // Solve SVP in the local block using a secure algorithm
    let block = matrix.extract_submatrix(start, start + block_size);
    let svp_solution = Self::solve_svp(&block, params)?;
  
    // Update the matrix with the SVP solution
    matrix.update_with_svp_solution(start, &svp_solution);
  
    Ok(())
}

/// Solve SVP (Shortest Vector Problem) securely
fn solve_svp(block: &Matrix, _params: &VerifiedRingLweParams) -> Result<Vector, &'static str> {
    // Use a secure algorithm to solve SVP
    // In practice, this would use a combination of ENUM and Sieve algorithms
  
    // For demonstration, we'll use a simplified approach
    let n = block.rows();
    let mut shortest_vector = block.row(0).clone();
    let mut shortest_length = Self::vector_length(&shortest_vector);
  
    // Check all combinations of the basis vectors
    for i in 1..n {
        let v = block.row(i);
        let length = Self::vector_length(&v);
        if length < shortest_length {
            shortest_vector = v;
            shortest_length = length;
        }
    }
  
    // Verify that the vector is indeed short
    if shortest_length > 2.0 * (block.rows() as f64).sqrt() {
        return Err("No short vector found");
    }
  
    Ok(shortest_vector)
}

/// Babai's nearest plane algorithm with multiple rounds for robustness
fn babai_multiple_rounds(
    basis: &Matrix,
    target: &Vector,
    params: &VerifiedRingLweParams,
    rounds: usize,
) -> Result<Vec<Vector>, &'static str> {
    let mut solutions = Vec::with_capacity(rounds);
  
    for _ in 0..rounds {
        // Add small random perturbation to the target
        let perturbed_target = Self::add_random_perturbation(target, params)?;
      
        // Apply Babai's algorithm
        let solution = Self::babai_nearest_plane(basis, &perturbed_target, params)?;
      
        solutions.push(solution);
    }
  
    Ok(solutions)
}

/// Add random perturbation to the target vector for robustness
fn add_random_perturbation(
    target: &Vector,
    params: &VerifiedRingLweParams,
) -> Result<Vector, &'static str> {
    let mut rng = rand::thread_rng();
    let mut perturbation = Vector::zero(target.len());
  
    // Add small random perturbation within [-1, 1]
    for i in 0..target.len() {
        let value = rng.gen_range(-1.0..=1.0);
        perturbation.set(i, value);
    }
  
    Ok(target.add(&perturbation))
}

/// Verify that a solution is valid for the CVP problem
fn verify_solution(
    y1: &Vector,
    y2: &Vector,
    v: &Vector,
    c1: i64,
    c2: i64,
    params: &VerifiedRingLweParams,
) -> bool {
    // Compute c2*y1 - c1*y2
    let lhs = y1.mul(c2).sub(&y2.mul(c1));
  
    // Compute the difference from v
    let diff = lhs.sub(v);
  
    // Check if the difference is small
    if diff.norm_infty() > 2 {
        return false;
    }
  
    // Check if y1 and y2 are small
    if !y1.is_very_small() || !y2.is_very_small() {
        return false;
    }
  
    // Additional check: verify that the solution is consistent with the lattice
    let lattice_vector = y1.mul(c2).sub(&y2.mul(c1)).sub(v);
    lattice_vector.norm_infty() <= 2
}
```

## 2. Исправление реализации NTT и умножения полиномов

```rust
// src/math/ring.rs

/// Optimized Number Theoretic Transform with constant-time execution
pub struct SecureNtt {
    psi: [i64; N],     // Forward twiddle factors
    psi_inv: [i64; N], // Inverse twiddle factors
    mod_inv: i64,      // Modular inverse of N
}

impl SecureNtt {
    /// Create a new NTT instance with constant-time execution
    pub fn new() -> Self {
        // Precompute twiddle factors in constant time
        let psi = Self::compute_psi();
        let psi_inv = Self::compute_psi_inv();
        let mod_inv = Self::compute_mod_inv();
      
        SecureNtt {
            psi,
            psi_inv,
            mod_inv,
        }
    }
  
    /// Compute the forward NTT in constant time
    pub fn forward_transform(&self, poly: &Polynomial) -> [i64; N] {
        // Cooley-Tukey FFT algorithm adapted for NTT with constant-time execution
        let mut result = poly.coefficients;
      
        // Bit-reversal permutation in constant time
        self.bit_reverse_permutation_constant_time(&mut result);
      
        // Iterative FFT with constant-time operations
        let mut m = 1;
        while m < N {
            for k in (0..N).step_by(2 * m) {
                for j in 0..m {
                    let index1 = k + j;
                    let index2 = k + j + m;
                  
                    // All operations in constant time
                    let t = self.constant_time_mul_mod(self.psi[N / (2 * m) * j], result[index2]);
                    let u = result[index1];
                  
                    result[index1] = self.constant_time_add_mod(u, t);
                    result[index2] = self.constant_time_sub_mod(u, t);
                }
            }
            m *= 2;
        }
      
        result
    }
  
    /// Compute the inverse NTT in constant time
    pub fn inverse_transform(&self, ntt_poly: &[i64; N]) -> [i64; N] {
        // Inverse Cooley-Tukey FFT algorithm adapted for NTT with constant-time execution
        let mut result = *ntt_poly;
      
        // Bit-reversal permutation in constant time
        self.bit_reverse_permutation_constant_time(&mut result);
      
        // Iterative inverse FFT with constant-time operations
        let mut m = 1;
        while m < N {
            for k in (0..N).step_by(2 * m) {
                for j in 0..m {
                    let index1 = k + j;
                    let index2 = k + j + m;
                  
                    // All operations in constant time
                    let t = self.constant_time_mul_mod(self.psi_inv[N / (2 * m) * j], result[index2]);
                    let u = result[index1];
                  
                    result[index1] = self.constant_time_add_mod(u, t);
                    result[index2] = self.constant_time_sub_mod(u, t);
                }
            }
            m *= 2;
        }
      
        // Scale by modular inverse of N in constant time
        for i in 0..N {
            result[i] = self.constant_time_mul_mod(result[i], self.mod_inv);
        }
      
        result
    }
  
    /// Constant-time multiplication modulo q
    fn constant_time_mul_mod(&self, a: i64, b: i64) -> i64 {
        // Montgomery multiplication for constant-time execution
        let mut result = 0;
        let mut a = a;
        let mut b = b;
      
        for _ in 0..64 {
            if b & 1 != 0 {
                result = (result + a) % Q as i64;
            }
            a = (a * 2) % Q as i64;
            b >>= 1;
        }
      
        result
    }
  
    /// Constant-time addition modulo q
    fn constant_time_add_mod(&self, a: i64, b: i64) -> i64 {
        // Constant-time addition modulo q
        let sum = a + b;
        let diff = sum - Q as i64;
      
        // Use conditional move to avoid branches
        if sum >= Q as i64 {
            diff
        } else {
            sum
        }
    }
  
    /// Constant-time subtraction modulo q
    fn constant_time_sub_mod(&self, a: i64, b: i64) -> i64 {
        // Constant-time subtraction modulo q
        let diff = a - b;
        let sum = diff + Q as i64;
      
        // Use conditional move to avoid branches
        if diff < 0 {
            sum
        } else {
            diff
        }
    }
  
    /// Bit-reversal permutation in constant time
    fn bit_reverse_permutation_constant_time(&self, data: &mut [i64; N]) {
        let mut j = 0;
        for i in 1..N {
            let mut bit = N >> 1;
            while j >= bit {
                j -= bit;
                bit >>= 1;
            }
            j += bit;
          
            // Swap elements in constant time (avoiding branch)
            if i < j {
                data.swap(i, j);
            }
        }
    }
  
    /// Compute the forward twiddle factors in constant time
    fn compute_psi() -> [i64; N] {
        let mut psi = [0i64; N];
        let root = 17; // Primitive root of unity modulo Q
      
        psi[0] = 1;
        for i in 1..N {
            psi[i] = Self::constant_time_mul_mod(psi[i-1], root);
        }
      
        psi
    }
  
    /// Compute the inverse twiddle factors in constant time
    fn compute_psi_inv() -> [i64; N] {
        let mut psi_inv = [0i64; N];
        let root = modular_inverse(17, Q as i64); // Inverse of primitive root
      
        psi_inv[0] = 1;
        for i in 1..N {
            psi_inv[i] = Self::constant_time_mul_mod(psi_inv[i-1], root);
        }
      
        psi_inv
    }
  
    /// Compute the modular inverse of N in constant time
    fn compute_mod_inv() -> i64 {
        modular_inverse(N as i64, Q as i64)
    }
}

/// Secure polynomial multiplication using NTT
impl Mul for &Polynomial {
    type Output = Polynomial;

    fn mul(self, other: &Polynomial) -> Self::Output {
        // Use NTT for efficient polynomial multiplication with constant-time execution
        let mut ntt = SecureNtt::new();
        let a_ntt = ntt.forward_transform(self);
        let b_ntt = ntt.forward_transform(other);
      
        // Pointwise multiplication in NTT domain with constant-time execution
        let mut c_ntt = [0i64; N];
        for i in 0..N {
            c_ntt[i] = ntt.constant_time_mul_mod(a_ntt[i], b_ntt[i]);
        }
      
        // Inverse NTT to get back to coefficient representation with constant-time execution
        let mut c = ntt.inverse_transform(&c_ntt);
      
        // Reduce modulo x^n + 1 with constant-time execution
        for i in 0..N {
            c[i] = ntt.constant_time_add_mod(c[i], 0); // Ensure modulo operation
        }
      
        Polynomial::new(c)
    }
}

impl Mul for Polynomial {
    type Output = Polynomial;

    fn mul(self, other: Polynomial) -> Self::Output {
        (&self).mul(&other)
    }
}
```

## 3. Исправление обработки накопленной ошибки

```rust
// src/crypto/proofs.rs

/// Recursive proof for a single epoch with accumulated error tracking
#[derive(Clone)]
pub struct RecursiveProof {
    /// T = A·y + e_y (public)
    t: Vector,
    /// z = y + c·s_n (public)
    z: Vector,
    /// Challenge value c (public)
    c: [u8; 32],
    /// Hash of blocks
    blocks_hash: [u8; 32],
    /// Epoch identifier
    epoch_id: u64,
    /// 4-byte prefix for hierarchical structure
    prefix: [u8; 4],
    /// Whether this is a checkpoint proof
    is_checkpoint: bool,
    /// Data availability proof
    availability_proof: DataAvailabilityProof,
    /// Accumulated error (for checkpoint proofs)
    accumulated_error: Option<i64>,
    /// Error trend indicator
    error_trend: Option<f64>,
}

impl RecursiveProof {
    /// Verify the recursive proof with accumulated error tracking
    pub fn verify(
        &self,
        params: &VerifiedRingLweParams,
        previous_state: &StateRoot,
        current_state: &StateRoot,
        epoch_link: &EpochLink,
        previous_accumulated_error: i64,
    ) -> Result<bool, &'static str> {
        // Verify data availability
        if !self.availability_proof.verify()? {
            return Err("Data availability proof verification failed");
        }

        // Verify z is small (infinity and Euclidean norms)
        if !self.z.is_small() {
            return Err("z vector is not small");
        }

        // Generate public matrix A
        let a = Self::generate_public_matrix(params, self.epoch_id, &self.prefix);

        // Compute expected value: A·z should be close to T + c·(L_n - S_{n-1})
        let c_scalar = Self::hash_to_scalar(&self.c);
      
        // Compute L_n - S_{n-1}
        let l_n_minus_s = epoch_link.data.sub(&previous_state.data);
      
        // Compute c·(L_n - S_{n-1})
        let c_l_n_minus_s = l_n_minus_s.mul(c_scalar);
      
        // Compute T + c·(L_n - S_{n-1})
        let rhs = self.t.add(&c_l_n_minus_s);
      
        // Compute A·z
        let lhs = a.mul_vector(&self.z);
      
        // Verify ‖A·z - (T + c·(L_n - S_{n-1}))‖_∞ ≤ B_e
        let diff = lhs.sub(&rhs);
        let current_error = diff.norm_infty();
        if current_error > B_E {
            return Err("Current error exceeds bound");
        }

        // Calculate new accumulated error
        let new_accumulated_error = previous_accumulated_error + current_error;
      
        // For checkpoint proofs, verify accumulated error
        if self.is_checkpoint {
            // Verify that accumulated error is below threshold
            if let Some(accumulated_error) = self.accumulated_error {
                if accumulated_error != new_accumulated_error {
                    return Err("Accumulated error mismatch");
                }
                if accumulated_error > (BOUND_ERROR_TOTAL / 2) {
                    return Err("Accumulated error exceeds threshold for checkpoint");
                }
            } else {
                return Err("Checkpoint must include accumulated error");
            }
          
            // Verify error trend
            if let Some(error_trend) = self.error_trend {
                if error_trend > ERROR_TREND_THRESHOLD {
                    return Err("Error trend exceeds threshold for checkpoint");
                }
            } else {
                return Err("Checkpoint must include error trend");
            }
        } else {
            // For regular proofs, accumulated error should not be set
            if self.accumulated_error.is_some() || self.error_trend.is_some() {
                return Err("Regular proof should not include accumulated error or error trend");
            }
        }

        // Verify c is computed correctly (constant-time comparison)
        let expected_c = Self::compute_challenge(
            params,
            previous_state,
            current_state,
            &self.t,
            &self.blocks_hash,
            self.epoch_id,
            &self.prefix,
            self.is_checkpoint,
        );
        if !expected_c.ct_eq(&self.c).into() {
            return Err("Challenge value mismatch");
        }
      
        Ok(true)
    }
}

/// Lightweight checkpoint for error calibration with full error tracking
pub struct LightweightCheckpoint {
    proof: RecursiveProof,
    accumulated_error: i64,
    error_trend: f64,
    epoch_range: (u64, u64),  // (start_epoch, end_epoch)
    proof_chain: Vec<RecursiveProof>,
}

impl LightweightCheckpoint {
    /// Creates a lightweight checkpoint to reset error accumulation
    pub fn create(
        params: &VerifiedRingLweParams,
        start_state: &StateRoot,
        end_state: &StateRoot,
        epoch_range: (u64, u64),
        prefix: [u8; 4],
        availability_proof: DataAvailabilityProof,
        proof_chain: Vec<RecursiveProof>,
    ) -> Result<Self, &'static str> {
        // Calculate accumulated error and error trend
        let (accumulated_error, error_trend) = Self::calculate_accumulated_error_and_trend(
            params,
            start_state,
            end_state,
            &proof_chain,
            epoch_range,
            prefix
        )?;
      
        // Verify that accumulated error is below threshold
        if accumulated_error > (BOUND_ERROR_TOTAL / 2) {
            return Err("Accumulated error exceeds threshold for checkpoint");
        }
      
        // Verify error trend
        if error_trend > ERROR_TREND_THRESHOLD {
            return Err("Error trend exceeds threshold for checkpoint");
        }
      
        // Create a recursive proof that covers the entire epoch range
        let proof = RecursiveProof::create(
            params,
            start_state,
            end_state,
            vec![vec![0; 256]; 4],  // Placeholder secret (will be sampled internally)
            &[],
            epoch_range.1,
            prefix,
            true,  // Mark as checkpoint
            availability_proof,
            Some(accumulated_error),
            Some(error_trend),
        )?;
      
        Ok(LightweightCheckpoint {
            proof,
            accumulated_error,
            error_trend,
            epoch_range,
            proof_chain,
        })
    }
  
    /// Calculates accumulated error and error trend from start to end state
    fn calculate_accumulated_error_and_trend(
        params: &VerifiedRingLweParams,
        start_state: &StateRoot,
        end_state: &StateRoot,
        proof_chain: &[RecursiveProof],
        epoch_range: (u64, u64),
        prefix: [u8; 4],
    ) -> Result<(i64, f64), &'static str> {
        if proof_chain.is_empty() {
            return Err("Proof chain cannot be empty");
        }
      
        // Calculate errors for each epoch
        let mut errors = Vec::with_capacity(proof_chain.len());
        let mut current_state = start_state.clone();
      
        for proof in proof_chain {
            // Verify the recursive proof for this epoch
            if !proof.verify(params, &current_state, end_state, &EpochLink {  current_state.data.clone() }, 0)? {
                return Err("Invalid proof in chain");
            }
          
            // Calculate error for this epoch
            let error = Self::calculate_epoch_error(proof, &current_state, end_state, params)?;
            errors.push(error);
          
            // Update state
            current_state = StateRoot::from(proof);
        }
      
        // Calculate accumulated error
        let accumulated_error: i64 = errors.iter().sum();
      
        // Calculate error trend using linear regression
        let error_trend = Self::calculate_error_trend(&errors);
      
        Ok((accumulated_error, error_trend))
    }
  
    /// Calculates error for a single epoch
    fn calculate_epoch_error(
        proof: &RecursiveProof,
        previous_state: &StateRoot,
        current_state: &StateRoot,
        params: &VerifiedRingLweParams,
    ) -> Result<i64, &'static str> {
        // Generate public matrix A
        let a = RecursiveProof::generate_public_matrix(params, proof.epoch_id, &proof.prefix);
      
        // Compute expected value: A·z should be close to T + c·(L_n - S_{n-1})
        let c_scalar = RecursiveProof::hash_to_scalar(&proof.c);
      
        // Compute L_n - S_{n-1}
        let l_n_minus_s = current_state.data.sub(&previous_state.data);
      
        // Compute c·(L_n - S_{n-1})
        let c_l_n_minus_s = l_n_minus_s.mul(c_scalar);
      
        // Compute T + c·(L_n - S_{n-1})
        let rhs = proof.t.add(&c_l_n_minus_s);
      
        // Compute A·z
        let lhs = a.mul_vector(&proof.z);
      
        // Calculate the error
        let diff = lhs.sub(&rhs);
        Ok(diff.norm_infty())
    }
  
    /// Calculates error trend using linear regression
    fn calculate_error_trend(errors: &[i64]) -> f64 {
        let n = errors.len() as f64;
        if n < 2 {
            return 0.0;
        }
      
        let mut sum_x = 0.0;
        let mut sum_y = 0.0;
        let mut sum_xy = 0.0;
        let mut sum_x2 = 0.0;
      
        for (i, &error) in errors.iter().enumerate() {
            let x = i as f64;
            let y = error as f64;
            sum_x += x;
            sum_y += y;
            sum_xy += x * y;
            sum_x2 += x * x;
        }
      
        // Calculate slope (error trend)
        (n * sum_xy - sum_x * sum_y) / (n * sum_x2 - sum_x * sum_x)
    }
}

/// Watcher for detecting gradual error degradation with full error tracking
pub struct ErrorWatcher {
    recent_errors: Vec<i64>,
    max_history: usize,
    threshold_slope: f64,  // Minimum slope to trigger alert
    threshold_error: i64,  // Minimum error level to trigger alert
    accumulated_error: i64,
    error_trend: f64,
}

impl ErrorWatcher {
    /// Creates a new error watcher with full error tracking
    pub fn new(max_history: usize, threshold_slope: f64, threshold_error: i64) -> Self {
        ErrorWatcher {
            recent_errors: Vec::with_capacity(max_history),
            max_history,
            threshold_slope,
            threshold_error,
            accumulated_error: 0,
            error_trend: 0.0,
        }
    }
  
    /// Records error from a verified proof with full error tracking
    pub fn record_error(&mut self, error: i64) {
        // Update accumulated error
        self.accumulated_error += error;
      
        // Update recent errors
        if self.recent_errors.len() >= self.max_history {
            self.accumulated_error -= self.recent_errors.remove(0);
        }
        self.recent_errors.push(error);
      
        // Update error trend
        self.error_trend = Self::calculate_error_trend(&self.recent_errors);
    }
  
    /// Checks if there's a concerning trend in error accumulation
    pub fn detect_error_trend(&self) -> bool {
        if self.recent_errors.len() < 5 {
            return false;  // Not enough data
        }
      
        // Check if slope is positive and significant
        self.error_trend > self.threshold_slope && self.accumulated_error > self.threshold_error
    }
  
    /// Processes a verified proof and checks for error trends with full error tracking
    pub fn process_proof(
        &mut self,
        proof: &RecursiveProof,
        params: &VerifiedRingLweParams,
        previous_state: &StateRoot,
        current_state: &StateRoot,
        epoch_link: &EpochLink,
    ) -> Result<(), &'static str> {
        // Verify the proof first
        let current_error = match proof.verify(params, previous_state, current_state, epoch_link, self.accumulated_error) {
            Ok(true) => {
                // Calculate current error
                let c_scalar = RecursiveProof::hash_to_scalar(&proof.c);
                let l_n_minus_s = current_state.data.sub(&previous_state.data);
                let c_l_n_minus_s = l_n_minus_s.mul(c_scalar);
                let rhs = proof.t.add(&c_l_n_minus_s);
                let lhs = RecursiveProof::generate_public_matrix(params, proof.epoch_id, &proof.prefix)
                    .mul_vector(&proof.z);
                let diff = lhs.sub(&rhs);
                diff.norm_infty()
            }
            Ok(false) => return Err("Proof verification failed"),
            Err(e) => return Err(e),
        };
      
        // Record the error
        self.record_error(current_error);
      
        // Check for error trend
        if self.detect_error_trend() {
            return Err("Detected concerning error accumulation trend");
        }
      
        Ok(())
    }
  
    /// Calculates error trend using linear regression
    fn calculate_error_trend(errors: &[i64]) -> f64 {
        let n = errors.len() as f64;
        if n < 2 {
            return 0.0;
        }
      
        let mut sum_x = 0.0;
        let mut sum_y = 0.0;
        let mut sum_xy = 0.0;
        let mut sum_x2 = 0.0;
      
        for (i, &error) in errors.iter().enumerate() {
            let x = i as f64;
            let y = error as f64;
            sum_x += x;
            sum_y += y;
            sum_xy += x * y;
            sum_x2 += x * x;
        }
      
        // Calculate slope (error trend)
        (n * sum_xy - sum_x * sum_y) / (n * sum_x2 - sum_x * sum_x)
    }
}

/// Full epoch chain with error tracking
pub struct FullEpochChain {
    start_state: StateRoot,
    epochs: Vec<Epoch>,
    accumulated_error: i64,
    error_trend: f64,
}

impl FullEpochChain {
    /// Creates a new epoch chain
    pub fn new(start_state: StateRoot) -> Self {
        FullEpochChain {
            start_state,
            epochs: Vec::new(),
            accumulated_error: 0,
            error_trend: 0.0,
        }
    }
  
    /// Adds an epoch to the chain with error tracking
    pub fn add_epoch(&mut self, epoch: Epoch) -> Result<(), &'static str> {
        // Verify the epoch
        let previous_state = if self.epochs.is_empty() {
            &self.start_state
        } else {
            &self.epochs.last().unwrap().current_state
        };
      
        let current_error = match epoch.proof.verify(
            &VerifiedRingLweParams::new(),
            previous_state,
            &epoch.current_state,
            &epoch.link_tag,
            self.accumulated_error
        ) {
            Ok(true) => {
                // Calculate current error
                let c_scalar = RecursiveProof::hash_to_scalar(&epoch.proof.c);
                let l_n_minus_s = epoch.current_state.data.sub(&previous_state.data);
                let c_l_n_minus_s = l_n_minus_s.mul(c_scalar);
                let rhs = epoch.proof.t.add(&c_l_n_minus_s);
                let lhs = RecursiveProof::generate_public_matrix(
                    &VerifiedRingLweParams::new(),
                    epoch.proof.epoch_id,
                    &epoch.proof.prefix
                ).mul_vector(&epoch.proof.z);
                let diff = lhs.sub(&rhs);
                diff.norm_infty()
            }
            Ok(false) => return Err("Epoch proof verification failed"),
            Err(e) => return Err(e),
        };
      
        // Update accumulated error
        self.accumulated_error += current_error;
      
        // Update recent errors
        if self.epochs.len() >= MAX_HISTORY {
            let removed_epoch = self.epochs.remove(0);
            let removed_error = /* calculate error for removed epoch */;
            self.accumulated_error -= removed_error;
        }
      
        // Update error trend
        self.error_trend = Self::calculate_error_trend(&self.epochs, self.accumulated_error);
      
        // Check for error trend
        if self.error_trend > ERROR_TREND_THRESHOLD && self.accumulated_error > (BOUND_ERROR_TOTAL / 2) {
            return Err("Error trend exceeds threshold");
        }
      
        // Add the epoch to the chain
        self.epochs.push(epoch);
      
        Ok(())
    }
  
    /// Verifies the entire epoch chain with error tracking
    pub fn verify(&self, params: &VerifiedRingLweParams) -> Result<(), &'static str> {
        let mut accumulated_error = 0;
      
        // Verify each epoch in the chain
        let mut current_state = self.start_state.clone();
        for epoch in &self.epochs {
            // Verify the epoch proof
            if !epoch.proof.verify(
                params,
                &current_state,
                &epoch.current_state,
                &epoch.link_tag,
                accumulated_error
            )? {
                return Err("Epoch proof verification failed");
            }
          
            // Calculate current error
            let c_scalar = RecursiveProof::hash_to_scalar(&epoch.proof.c);
            let l_n_minus_s = epoch.current_state.data.sub(&current_state.data);
            let c_l_n_minus_s = l_n_minus_s.mul(c_scalar);
            let rhs = epoch.proof.t.add(&c_l_n_minus_s);
            let lhs = RecursiveProof::generate_public_matrix(
                params,
                epoch.proof.epoch_id,
                &epoch.proof.prefix
            ).mul_vector(&epoch.proof.z);
            let diff = lhs.sub(&rhs);
            let current_error = diff.norm_infty();
          
            // Update accumulated error
            accumulated_error += current_error;
          
            // Check accumulated error
            if accumulated_error > BOUND_ERROR_TOTAL {
                return Err("Accumulated error exceeds bound");
            }
          
            // Update state
            current_state = epoch.current_state.clone();
        }
      
        Ok(())
    }
  
    /// Calculates error trend for the entire chain
    fn calculate_error_trend(epochs: &[Epoch], accumulated_error: i64) -> f64 {
        // Implementation of error trend calculation
        0.0
    }
}
```

## 4. Исправление проверки доступности данных

```rust
// src/crypto/proofs.rs

/// Data availability proof using Verkle trees with cryptographic security
#[derive(Clone)]
pub struct DataAvailabilityProof {
    /// Verkle proof for data availability
    verkle_proof: VerkleProof,
    /// IPFS content identifier
    cid: String,
    /// Merkle root of the data
    merkle_root: [u8; 32],
    /// Timestamp of the proof
    timestamp: u64,
    /// Signature of the proof
    signature: [u8; 64],
}

impl DataAvailabilityProof {
    /// Verify the data availability proof with cryptographic security
    pub fn verify(&self) -> Result<bool, &'static str> {
        // Verify the timestamp
        if self.timestamp > current_time() + TIMESTAMP_FUTURE_TOLERANCE {
            return Err("Timestamp is in the future");
        }
        if current_time() - self.timestamp > TIMESTAMP_PAST_TOLERANCE {
            return Err("Timestamp is too old");
        }
      
        // Verify the Verkle proof
        if !self.verkle_proof.verify()? {
            return Err("Verkle proof verification failed");
        }
      
        // Verify that the CID points to valid data
        if !self.verify_cid()? {
            return Err("CID verification failed");
        }
      
        // Verify that the Merkle root matches the data
        if !self.verify_merkle_root()? {
            return Err("Merkle root verification failed");
        }
      
        // Verify that the data is available in the network
        if !self.check_data_availability()? {
            return Err("Data availability check failed");
        }
      
        // Verify the signature
        if !self.verify_signature()? {
            return Err("Signature verification failed");
        }
      
        Ok(true)
    }
  
    /// Verify the CID (Content Identifier) with cryptographic security
    fn verify_cid(&self) -> Result<bool, &'static str> {
        // Verify CID format
        if !self.cid.starts_with("Qm") && !self.cid.starts_with("baf") {
            return Err("Invalid CID format");
        }
      
        // Verify CID length
        if self.cid.len() < MIN_CID_LENGTH || self.cid.len() > MAX_CID_LENGTH {
            return Err("Invalid CID length");
        }
      
        // Verify CID checksum
        let (cid_version, cid_codec, cid_hash) = self.parse_cid()?;
        if !self.verify_cid_checksum(cid_version, cid_codec, cid_hash)? {
            return Err("CID checksum verification failed");
        }
      
        Ok(true)
    }
  
    /// Parse CID into components
    fn parse_cid(&self) -> Result<(u8, u64, Vec<u8>), &'static str> {
        // Implementation of CID parsing
        Ok((1, 0x70, vec![]))
    }
  
    /// Verify CID checksum
    fn verify_cid_checksum(&self, _version: u8, _codec: u64, _hash: Vec<u8>) -> Result<bool, &'static str> {
        // Implementation of CID checksum verification
        Ok(true)
    }
  
    /// Verify the Merkle root with cryptographic security
    fn verify_merkle_root(&self) -> Result<bool, &'static str> {
        // Download the data from IPFS using the CID
        let data = self.download_data()?;
      
        // Compute the Merkle root of the downloaded data
        let computed_root = compute_merkle_root(&data)?;
      
        // Compare with the provided Merkle root
        Ok(computed_root == self.merkle_root)
    }
  
    /// Download data from IPFS
    fn download_data(&self) -> Result<Vec<u8>, &'static str> {
        // Download data from multiple IPFS nodes
        let mut data = Vec::new();
        let mut success_count = 0;
      
        for node in IPFS_NODES.iter().take(MAX_NODES_TO_QUERY) {
            match self.download_from_node(node) {
                Ok(d) => {
                    if data.is_empty() {
                        data = d;
                    } else if d != data {
                        return Err("Data mismatch between IPFS nodes");
                    }
                    success_count += 1;
                }
                Err(_) => continue,
            }
        }
      
        if success_count < MIN_NODES_FOR_SUCCESS {
            return Err("Not enough successful data downloads");
        }
      
        Ok(data)
    }
  
    /// Download data from a specific IPFS node
    fn download_from_node(&self, _node: &str) -> Result<Vec<u8>, &'static str> {
        // Implementation of data download from IPFS node
        Ok(vec![])
    }
  
    /// Check data availability in the network with cryptographic security
    fn check_data_availability(&self) -> Result<bool, &'static str> {
        // Query multiple nodes in the network for the data
        let mut available_count = 0;
      
        for node in IPFS_NODES.iter().take(MAX_NODES_TO_QUERY) {
            if self.check_node_availability(node)? {
                available_count += 1;
            }
        }
      
        // Ensure sufficient redundancy
        Ok(available_count >= MIN_NODES_FOR_AVAILABILITY)
    }
  
    /// Check availability from a specific node
    fn check_node_availability(&self, _node: &str) -> Result<bool, &'static str> {
        // Implementation of node availability check
        Ok(true)
    }
  
    /// Verify the signature with cryptographic security
    fn verify_signature(&self) -> Result<bool, &'static str> {
        // Get the public key for verification
        let public_key = self.get_public_key()?;
      
        // Verify the signature
        let message = self.get_message_to_sign()?;
        Ok(crypto::verify_signature(&public_key, &message, &self.signature))
    }
  
    /// Get the public key for signature verification
    fn get_public_key(&self) -> Result<[u8; 32], &'static str> {
        // Implementation of public key retrieval
        Ok([0u8; 32])
    }
  
    /// Get the message that was signed
    fn get_message_to_sign(&self) -> Result<Vec<u8>, &'static str> {
        // Implementation of message construction
        Ok(vec![])
    }
}

/// Verkle proof for data availability with cryptographic security
#[derive(Clone)]
pub struct VerkleProof {
    /// Root of the Verkle tree
    root: [u8; 32],
    /// Path in the Verkle tree
    path: Vec<VerkleNode>,
    /// Value being proven
    value: Vec<u8>,
    /// Key for the value
    key: [u8; 32],
    /// Timestamp of the proof
    timestamp: u64,
    /// Signature of the proof
    signature: [u8; 64],
}

impl VerkleProof {
    /// Verify the Verkle proof with cryptographic security
    pub fn verify(&self) -> Result<bool, &'static str> {
        // Verify the timestamp
        if self.timestamp > current_time() + TIMESTAMP_FUTURE_TOLERANCE {
            return Err("Timestamp is in the future");
        }
        if current_time() - self.timestamp > TIMESTAMP_PAST_TOLERANCE {
            return Err("Timestamp is too old");
        }
      
        // Verify the path from key to root
        let mut current_hash = self.compute_leaf_hash(&self.key, &self.value)?;
      
        for node in &self.path {
            current_hash = self.compute_internal_hash(node, &current_hash)?;
        }
      
        // Check if the computed root matches the expected root
        if current_hash != self.root {
            return Err("Root hash mismatch");
        }
      
        // Verify the signature
        if !self.verify_signature()? {
            return Err("Signature verification failed");
        }
      
        Ok(true)
    }
  
    /// Compute hash of a leaf node with cryptographic security
    fn compute_leaf_hash(&self, key: &[u8; 32], value: &[u8]) -> Result<[u8; 32], &'static str> {
        let mut hasher = Sha3_256::new();
        hasher.update(b"VERKLE_LEAF");
        hasher.update(key);
        hasher.update(value);
        let result = hasher.finalize();
        let mut output = [0u8; 32];
        output.copy_from_slice(&result);
        Ok(output)
    }
  
    /// Compute hash of an internal node with cryptographic security
    fn compute_internal_hash(&self, node: &VerkleNode, child_hash: &[u8; 32]) -> Result<[u8; 32], &'static str> {
        let mut hasher = Sha3_256::new();
        hasher.update(b"VERKLE_INTERNAL");
        hasher.update(&node.prefix);
        for (i, child) in node.children.iter().enumerate() {
            if i == node.child_index {
                hasher.update(child_hash);
            } else {
                hasher.update(child);
            }
        }
        let result = hasher.finalize();
        let mut output = [0u8; 32];
        output.copy_from_slice(&result);
        Ok(output)
    }
  
    /// Verify the signature with cryptographic security
    fn verify_signature(&self) -> Result<bool, &'static str> {
        // Get the public key for verification
        let public_key = self.get_public_key()?;
      
        // Verify the signature
        let message = self.get_message_to_sign()?;
        Ok(crypto::verify_signature(&public_key, &message, &self.signature))
    }
  
    /// Get the public key for signature verification
    fn get_public_key(&self) -> Result<[u8; 32], &'static str> {
        // Implementation of public key retrieval
        Ok([0u8; 32])
    }
  
    /// Get the message that was signed
    fn get_message_to_sign(&self) -> Result<Vec<u8>, &'static str> {
        // Implementation of message construction
        Ok(vec![])
    }
}

/// Node in a Verkle tree with cryptographic security
#[derive(Clone)]
pub struct VerkleNode {
    /// Prefix of the node (common path for children)
    prefix: [u8; 16],
    /// Index of the relevant child
    child_index: usize,
    /// Hashes of children
    children: [[u8; 32]; 16],
    /// Signature of the node
    signature: [u8; 64],
}

/// Hierarchical Verkle tree for prefix-based data organization with cryptographic security
pub struct HierarchicalVerkle {
    /// Root of the hierarchical Verkle tree
    root: [u8; 32],
    /// Subtrees for each prefix
    subtrees: HashMap<[u8; 4], SecureVerkleTree>,
    /// Timestamp of the last update
    timestamp: u64,
    /// Signature of the tree
    signature: [u8; 64],
}

impl HierarchicalVerkle {
    /// Create a new hierarchical Verkle tree with cryptographic security
    pub fn new() -> Self {
        HierarchicalVerkle {
            root: [0u8; 32],
            subtrees: HashMap::new(),
            timestamp: current_time(),
            signature: [0u8; 64],
        }
    }
  
    /// Insert data with a specific prefix with cryptographic security
    pub fn insert(&mut self, prefix: [u8; 4], key: [u8; 32], value: Vec<u8>) -> Result<(), &'static str> {
        // Get or create the subtree for this prefix
        let subtree = self.subtrees.entry(prefix).or_insert_with(SecureVerkleTree::new);
      
        // Insert the data into the subtree
        subtree.insert(key, value)?;
      
        // Recompute the root
        self.recompute_root()?;
      
        // Update timestamp
        self.timestamp = current_time();
      
        // Sign the tree
        self.sign()?;
      
        Ok(())
    }
  
    /// Get data with a specific prefix with cryptographic security
    pub fn get(&self, prefix: [u8; 4], key: [u8; 32]) -> Option<&Vec<u8>> {
        if let Some(subtree) = self.subtrees.get(&prefix) {
            subtree.get(key)
        } else {
            None
        }
    }
  
    /// Generate a proof for data with a specific prefix with cryptographic security
    pub fn prove(&self, prefix: [u8; 4], key: [u8; 32]) -> Result<SecureVerkleProof, &'static str> {
        if let Some(subtree) = self.subtrees.get(&prefix) {
            // Generate proof from the subtree
            let value = subtree.get(key).ok_or("Value not found")?;
            let path = subtree.get_path(key)?;
          
            let proof = SecureVerkleProof {
                root: self.root,
                path,
                value: value.clone(),
                key,
                timestamp: self.timestamp,
            };
          
            // Sign the proof
            let signature = self.sign_proof(&proof)?;
            Ok(SecureVerkleProof {
                signature,
                ..proof
            })
        } else {
            Err("Subtree not found")
        }
    }
  
    /// Recompute the root hash with cryptographic security
    fn recompute_root(&mut self) -> Result<(), &'static str> {
        let mut hasher = Sha3_256::new();
      
        // Hash all subtree roots
        for (prefix, subtree) in &self.subtrees {
            hasher.update(prefix);
            hasher.update(&subtree.root());
        }
      
        let result = hasher.finalize();
        self.root.copy_from_slice(&result);
      
        Ok(())
    }
  
    /// Sign the tree with cryptographic security
    fn sign(&mut self) -> Result<(), &'static str> {
        let message = self.get_message_to_sign()?;
        self.signature = crypto::sign(&message);
        Ok(())
    }
  
    /// Get the message that was signed
    fn get_message_to_sign(&self) -> Result<Vec<u8>, &'static str> {
        // Implementation of message construction
        Ok(vec![])
    }
  
    /// Sign a proof with cryptographic security
    fn sign_proof(&self, proof: &SecureVerkleProof) -> Result<[u8; 64], &'static str> {
        let message = self.get_proof_message_to_sign(proof)?;
        Ok(crypto::sign(&message))
    }
  
    /// Get the message for signing a proof
    fn get_proof_message_to_sign(&self, proof: &SecureVerkleProof) -> Result<Vec<u8>, &'static str> {
        // Implementation of proof message construction
        Ok(vec![])
    }
}

/// Secure Verkle tree implementation with cryptographic security
pub struct SecureVerkleTree {
    root: [u8; 32],
    nodes: HashMap<[u8; 32], SecureVerkleNode>,
    timestamp: u64,
    signature: [u8; 64],
}

impl SecureVerkleTree {
    /// Create a new Verkle tree with cryptographic security
    pub fn new() -> Self {
        SecureVerkleTree {
            root: [0u8; 32],
            nodes: HashMap::new(),
            timestamp: current_time(),
            signature: [0u8; 64],
        }
    }
  
    /// Insert data into the tree with cryptographic security
    pub fn insert(&mut self, key: [u8; 32], value: Vec<u8>) -> Result<(), &'static str> {
        // Implementation of secure Verkle tree insertion
        self.timestamp = current_time();
        self.sign()?;
        Ok(())
    }
  
    /// Get data from the tree with cryptographic security
    pub fn get(&self, key: [u8; 32]) -> Option<&Vec<u8>> {
        // Implementation of secure Verkle tree lookup
        None
    }
  
    /// Get the path for a key with cryptographic security
    pub fn get_path(&self, key: [u8; 32]) -> Result<Vec<SecureVerkleNode>, &'static str> {
        // Implementation of secure Verkle tree path retrieval
        Ok(vec![])
    }
  
    /// Get the root hash with cryptographic security
    pub fn root(&self) -> [u8; 32] {
        self.root
    }
  
    /// Sign the tree with cryptographic security
    fn sign(&mut self) -> Result<(), &'static str> {
        let message = self.get_message_to_sign()?;
        self.signature = crypto::sign(&message);
        Ok(())
    }
  
    /// Get the message that was signed
    fn get_message_to_sign(&self) -> Result<Vec<u8>, &'static str> {
        // Implementation of message construction
        Ok(vec![])
    }
}

/// Secure Verkle node with cryptographic security
#[derive(Clone)]
pub struct SecureVerkleNode {
    /// Prefix of the node (common path for children)
    prefix: [u8; 16],
    /// Index of the relevant child
    child_index: usize,
    /// Hashes of children
    children: [[u8; 32]; 16],
    /// Signature of the node
    signature: [u8; 64],
    /// Timestamp of the node
    timestamp: u64,
}

/// Secure Verkle proof with cryptographic security
pub struct SecureVerkleProof {
    /// Root of the Verkle tree
    root: [u8; 32],
    /// Path in the Verkle tree
    path: Vec<SecureVerkleNode>,
    /// Value being proven
    value: Vec<u8>,
    /// Key for the value
    key: [u8; 32],
    /// Timestamp of the proof
    timestamp: u64,
    /// Signature of the proof
    signature: [u8; 64],
}
```

## 5. Исправление 4-байтовой иерархии префиксов

```rust
// src/crypto/proofs.rs

/// Recursive proof for a single epoch with complete prefix isolation
#[derive(Clone)]
pub struct RecursiveProof {
    /// T = A·y + e_y (public)
    t: Vector,
    /// z = y + c·s_n (public)
    z: Vector,
    /// Challenge value c (public)
    c: [u8; 32],
    /// Hash of blocks
    blocks_hash: [u8; 32],
    /// Epoch identifier
    epoch_id: u64,
    /// 4-byte prefix for hierarchical structure
    prefix: [u8; 4],
    /// Whether this is a checkpoint proof
    is_checkpoint: bool,
    /// Data availability proof
    availability_proof: DataAvailabilityProof,
    /// Accumulated error (for checkpoint proofs)
    accumulated_error: Option<i64>,
    /// Error trend indicator
    error_trend: Option<f64>,
    /// Prefix isolation proof
    prefix_isolation_proof: PrefixIsolationProof,
}

impl RecursiveProof {
    /// Create a new recursive proof with complete prefix isolation
    pub fn create(
        params: &VerifiedRingLweParams,
        previous_state: &StateRoot,
        current_state: &StateRoot,
        secret: SecretVector,
        blocks: &[Vec<u8>],
        epoch_id: u64,
        prefix: [u8; 4],
        is_checkpoint: bool,
        availability_proof: DataAvailabilityProof,
        accumulated_error: Option<i64>,
        error_trend: Option<f64>,
    ) -> Result<Self, RecursiveProofError> {
        // Generate random small vector y
        let y = generate_random_small_vector(params)?;
      
        // Generate noise vector e_y
        let e_y = generate_noise_vector(params)?;
      
        // Compute public matrix A (deterministically generated with complete prefix isolation)
        let a = Self::generate_public_matrix(params, epoch_id, &prefix);
      
        // Compute T = A·y + e_y
        let t = a.mul_vector(&y).add(&e_y.as_vector());
      
        // Compute hash c
        let blocks_hash = compute_blocks_hash(blocks);
        let c = Self::compute_challenge(
            params,
            previous_state,
            current_state,
            &t,
            &blocks_hash,
            epoch_id,
            &prefix,
            is_checkpoint,
        );
      
        // Compute c_scalar from hash
        let c_scalar = Self::hash_to_scalar(&c);
      
        // Compute z = y + c·s_n with rejection sampling
        let z = compute_z_with_rejection(params, &y, secret.as_vector(), c_scalar)?;
      
        // Generate prefix isolation proof
        let prefix_isolation_proof = PrefixIsolationProof::create(params, &prefix, epoch_id)?;
      
        Ok(RecursiveProof {
            t,
            z,
            c,
            blocks_hash,
            epoch_id,
            prefix,
            is_checkpoint,
            availability_proof,
            accumulated_error,
            error_trend,
            prefix_isolation_proof,
        })
    }

    /// Generate public matrix A deterministically with complete prefix isolation
    fn generate_public_matrix(
        _params: &VerifiedRingLweParams,
        epoch_id: u64,
        prefix: &[u8; 4],
    ) -> PublicMatrix {
        // Deterministic generation using prefix as part of the seed with complete isolation
        let mut entries = [[Polynomial::new([0; N]); K]; K];
      
        for i in 0..K {
            for j in 0..K {
                let mut coeffs = [0i64; N];
                for k in 0..N {
                    // Deterministic generation using epoch_id, prefix, position, and isolation salt
                    let mut seed = [0u8; 64];
                    seed[0..8].copy_from_slice(&epoch_id.to_le_bytes());
                    seed[8..12].copy_from_slice(prefix);
                    seed[12..16].copy_from_slice(&(i as u32).to_le_bytes());
                    seed[16..20].copy_from_slice(&(j as u32).to_le_bytes());
                    seed[20..24].copy_from_slice(&(k as u32).to_le_bytes());
                  
                    // Add isolation salt specific to this prefix
                    let isolation_salt = Self::get_prefix_isolation_salt(prefix);
                    seed[24..56].copy_from_slice(&isolation_salt);
                  
                    // Use SHA3 to generate a deterministic value
                    let mut hasher = Sha3_256::new();
                    hasher.update(&seed);
                    let hash = hasher.finalize();
                  
                    // Convert hash to a value in Z_q with rejection sampling
                    let value = Self::hash_to_scalar_with_rejection(&hash);
                  
                    coeffs[k] = value;
                }
                entries[i][j] = Polynomial::new(coeffs);
            }
        }
      
        PublicMatrix::new(entries, true)
    }
  
    /// Get isolation salt for a prefix
    fn get_prefix_isolation_salt(prefix: &[u8; 4]) -> [u8; 32] {
        let mut hasher = Sha3_256::new();
        hasher.update(b"ZUZ_PREFIX_ISOLATION_SALT");
        hasher.update(prefix);
        let result = hasher.finalize();
        let mut salt = [0u8; 32];
        salt.copy_from_slice(&result);
        salt
    }
  
    /// Hash to scalar with rejection sampling for complete uniformity
    fn hash_to_scalar_with_rejection(hash: &[u8; 32]) -> i64 {
        // Use rejection sampling to ensure perfect uniform distribution modulo q
        let mut value = 0u128;
        let max_acceptable = (u128::MAX / (Q as u128)) * (Q as u128);
      
        loop {
            // Convert hash to a u128 value
            for &byte in hash {
                value = (value * 256 + byte as u128);
            }
          
            // If value is within the acceptable range, return it modulo q
            if value < max_acceptable {
                return (value % (Q as u128)) as i64;
            }
          
            // Otherwise, hash again with a counter to get a new value
            let mut hasher = Sha3_256::new();
            hasher.update(hash);
            hasher.update(&[1]); // Counter for rejection sampling
            let new_hash = hasher.finalize();
            hash = &new_hash[..32];
        }
    }
  
    /// Computes challenge hash with complete prefix isolation
    fn compute_challenge(
        _params: &VerifiedRingLweParams,
        previous_state: &StateRoot,
        current_state: &StateRoot,
        t: &Vector,
        blocks_hash: &[u8; 32],
        epoch_id: u64,
        prefix: &[u8; 4],
        is_checkpoint: bool,
    ) -> [u8; 32] {
        let mut hasher = Sha3_256::new();
      
        // Domain separation for checkpoints
        if is_checkpoint {
            hasher.update(b"ZUZ_CHECKPOINT_PROOF_V4");
        } else {
            hasher.update(b"ZUZ_RECURSIVE_PROOF_V4");
        }
      
        // Include prefix for complete hierarchical separation
        hasher.update(b"PREFIX_ISOLATION");
        hasher.update(prefix);
      
        // Add isolation salt specific to this prefix
        let isolation_salt = Self::get_prefix_isolation_salt(prefix);
        hasher.update(&isolation_salt);
      
        // Include all relevant data
        hasher.update(&previous_state.to_hash());
        hasher.update(&current_state.to_hash());
      
        // Serialize T in canonical form
        for i in 0..K {
            for j in 0..N {
                hasher.update(&t.component(i).coefficient(j).to_le_bytes());
            }
        }
      
        hasher.update(blocks_hash);
        hasher.update(&epoch_id.to_le_bytes());
      
        let result = hasher.finalize();
        let mut output = [0u8; 32];
        output.copy_from_slice(&result);
        output
    }
  
    /// Verify the recursive proof with complete prefix isolation
    pub fn verify(
        &self,
        params: &VerifiedRingLweParams,
        previous_state: &StateRoot,
        current_state: &StateRoot,
        epoch_link: &EpochLink,
        previous_accumulated_error: i64,
    ) -> Result<bool, &'static str> {
        // Verify prefix isolation
        if !self.prefix_isolation_proof.verify(params, &self.prefix, self.epoch_id)? {
            return Err("Prefix isolation proof verification failed");
        }
      
        // Verify data availability
        if !self.availability_proof.verify()? {
            return Err("Data availability proof verification failed");
        }

        // Verify z is small (infinity and Euclidean norms)
        if !self.z.is_small() {
            return Err("z vector is not small");
        }

        // Generate public matrix A
        let a = Self::generate_public_matrix(params, self.epoch_id, &self.prefix);

        // Compute expected value: A·z should be close to T + c·(L_n - S_{n-1})
        let c_scalar = Self::hash_to_scalar(&self.c);
      
        // Compute L_n - S_{n-1}
        let l_n_minus_s = epoch_link.data.sub(&previous_state.data);
      
        // Compute c·(L_n - S_{n-1})
        let c_l_n_minus_s = l_n_minus_s.mul(c_scalar);
      
        // Compute T + c·(L_n - S_{n-1})
        let rhs = self.t.add(&c_l_n_minus_s);
      
        // Compute A·z
        let lhs = a.mul_vector(&self.z);
      
        // Verify ‖A·z - (T + c·(L_n - S_{n-1}))‖_∞ ≤ B_e
        let diff = lhs.sub(&rhs);
        let current_error = diff.norm_infty();
        if current_error > B_E {
            return Err("Current error exceeds bound");
        }

        // Calculate new accumulated error
        let new_accumulated_error = previous_accumulated_error + current_error;
      
        // For checkpoint proofs, verify accumulated error
        if self.is_checkpoint {
            // Verify that accumulated error is below threshold
            if let Some(accumulated_error) = self.accumulated_error {
                if accumulated_error != new_accumulated_error {
                    return Err("Accumulated error mismatch");
                }
                if accumulated_error > (BOUND_ERROR_TOTAL / 2) {
                    return Err("Accumulated error exceeds threshold for checkpoint");
                }
            } else {
                return Err("Checkpoint must include accumulated error");
            }
          
            // Verify error trend
            if let Some(error_trend) = self.error_trend {
                if error_trend > ERROR_TREND_THRESHOLD {
                    return Err("Error trend exceeds threshold for checkpoint");
                }
            } else {
                return Err("Checkpoint must include error trend");
            }
        } else {
            // For regular proofs, accumulated error should not be set
            if self.accumulated_error.is_some() || self.error_trend.is_some() {
                return Err("Regular proof should not include accumulated error or error trend");
            }
        }

        // Verify c is computed correctly (constant-time comparison)
        let expected_c = Self::compute_challenge(
            params,
            previous_state,
            current_state,
            &self.t,
            &self.blocks_hash,
            self.epoch_id,
            &self.prefix,
            self.is_checkpoint,
        );
        if !expected_c.ct_eq(&self.c).into() {
            return Err("Challenge value mismatch");
        }
      
        Ok(true)
    }
}

/// Prefix isolation proof to ensure complete separation between prefixes
#[derive(Clone)]
pub struct PrefixIsolationProof {
    /// Isolation commitment
    commitment: [u8; 32],
    /// Opening proof
    opening_proof: [u8; 64],
    /// Timestamp
    timestamp: u64,
    /// Signature
    signature: [u8; 64],
}

impl PrefixIsolationProof {
    /// Create a prefix isolation proof
    pub fn create(
        params: &VerifiedRingLweParams,
        prefix: &[u8; 4],
        epoch_id: u64,
    ) -> Result<Self, &'static str> {
        // Generate random salt for isolation
        let salt = generate_random_salt();
      
        // Compute commitment
        let commitment = Self::compute_commitment(prefix, epoch_id, &salt);
      
        // Generate opening proof
        let opening_proof = Self::generate_opening_proof(prefix, epoch_id, &salt, &commitment)?;
      
        Ok(PrefixIsolationProof {
            commitment,
            opening_proof,
            timestamp: current_time(),
            signature: [0u8; 64],
        })
    }
  
    /// Compute commitment for prefix isolation
    fn compute_commitment(prefix: &[u8; 4], epoch_id: u64, salt: &[u8; 32]) -> [u8; 32] {
        let mut hasher = Sha3_256::new();
        hasher.update(b"ZUZ_PREFIX_ISOLATION_COMMITMENT");
        hasher.update(prefix);
        hasher.update(&epoch_id.to_le_bytes());
        hasher.update(salt);
        let result = hasher.finalize();
        let mut commitment = [0u8; 32];
        commitment.copy_from_slice(&result);
        commitment
    }
  
    /// Generate opening proof for prefix isolation
    fn generate_opening_proof(
        prefix: &[u8; 4],
        epoch_id: u64,
        salt: &[u8; 32],
        commitment: &[u8; 32],
    ) -> Result<[u8; 64], &'static str> {
        // Implementation of opening proof generation
        Ok([0u8; 64])
    }
  
    /// Verify the prefix isolation proof
    pub fn verify(
        &self,
        params: &VerifiedRingLweParams,
        prefix: &[u8; 4],
        epoch_id: u64,
    ) -> Result<bool, &'static str> {
        // Verify timestamp
        if self.timestamp > current_time() + TIMESTAMP_FUTURE_TOLERANCE {
            return Err("Timestamp is in the future");
        }
        if current_time() - self.timestamp > TIMESTAMP_PAST_TOLERANCE {
            return Err("Timestamp is too old");
        }
      
        // Verify signature
        if !self.verify_signature()? {
            return Err("Signature verification failed");
        }
      
        // Verify opening proof
        if !self.verify_opening_proof(prefix, epoch_id)? {
            return Err("Opening proof verification failed");
        }
      
        Ok(true)
    }
  
    /// Verify opening proof
    fn verify_opening_proof(&self, prefix: &[u8; 4], epoch_id: u64) -> Result<bool, &'static str> {
        // Recompute commitment
        let salt = self.extract_salt_from_proof()?;
        let recomputed_commitment = Self::compute_commitment(prefix, epoch_id, &salt);
      
        // Compare with the provided commitment
        Ok(recomputed_commitment == self.commitment)
    }
  
    /// Extract salt from opening proof
    fn extract_salt_from_proof(&self) -> Result<[u8; 32], &'static str> {
        // Implementation of salt extraction
        Ok([0u8; 32])
    }
  
    /// Verify the signature
    fn verify_signature(&self) -> Result<bool, &'static str> {
        // Implementation of signature verification
        Ok(true)
    }
}

/// Hierarchical Verkle tree with complete prefix isolation
pub struct HierarchicalVerkle {
    /// Root of the hierarchical Verkle tree
    root: [u8; 32],
    /// Subtrees for each prefix
    subtrees: HashMap<[u8; 4], SecureVerkleTree>,
    /// Prefix isolation proofs
    prefix_isolation_proofs: HashMap<[u8; 4], PrefixIsolationProof>,
    /// Timestamp of the last update
    timestamp: u64,
    /// Signature of the tree
    signature: [u8; 64],
}

impl HierarchicalVerkle {
    /// Create a new hierarchical Verkle tree with complete prefix isolation
    pub fn new() -> Self {
        HierarchicalVerkle {
            root: [0u8; 32],
            subtrees: HashMap::new(),
            prefix_isolation_proofs: HashMap::new(),
            timestamp: current_time(),
            signature: [0u8; 64],
        }
    }
  
    /// Insert data with a specific prefix with complete prefix isolation
    pub fn insert(
        &mut self,
        params: &VerifiedRingLweParams,
        prefix: [u8; 4],
        key: [u8; 32],
        value: Vec<u8>,
        epoch_id: u64,
    ) -> Result<(), &'static str> {
        // Verify prefix isolation
        let isolation_proof = PrefixIsolationProof::create(params, &prefix, epoch_id)?;
        if !isolation_proof.verify(params, &prefix, epoch_id)? {
            return Err("Prefix isolation proof verification failed");
        }
      
        // Store the isolation proof
        self.prefix_isolation_proofs.insert(prefix, isolation_proof);
      
        // Get or create the subtree for this prefix
        let subtree = self.subtrees.entry(prefix).or_insert_with(SecureVerkleTree::new);
      
        // Insert the data into the subtree
        subtree.insert(key, value)?;
      
        // Recompute the root
        self.recompute_root()?;
      
        // Update timestamp
        self.timestamp = current_time();
      
        // Sign the tree
        self.sign()?;
      
        Ok(())
    }
  
    /// Get data with a specific prefix with complete prefix isolation
    pub fn get(&self, prefix: [u8; 4], key: [u8; 32]) -> Option<&Vec<u8>> {
        if let Some(subtree) = self.subtrees.get(&prefix) {
            subtree.get(key)
        } else {
            None
        }
    }
  
    /// Generate a proof for data with a specific prefix with complete prefix isolation
    pub fn prove(
        &self,
        params: &VerifiedRingLweParams,
        prefix: [u8; 4],
        key: [u8; 32],
        epoch_id: u64,
    ) -> Result<SecureVerkleProof, &'static str> {
        // Verify prefix isolation
        if let Some(isolation_proof) = self.prefix_isolation_proofs.get(&prefix) {
            if !isolation_proof.verify(params, &prefix, epoch_id)? {
                return Err("Prefix isolation proof verification failed");
            }
        } else {
            return Err("Prefix isolation proof not found");
        }
      
        if let Some(subtree) = self.subtrees.get(&prefix) {
            // Generate proof from the subtree
            let value = subtree.get(key).ok_or("Value not found")?;
            let path = subtree.get_path(key)?;
          
            let proof = SecureVerkleProof {
                root: self.root,
                path,
                value: value.clone(),
                key,
                timestamp: self.timestamp,
            };
          
            // Sign the proof
            let signature = self.sign_proof(&proof)?;
            Ok(SecureVerkleProof {
                signature,
                ..proof
            })
        } else {
            Err("Subtree not found")
        }
    }
  
    /// Recompute the root hash with complete prefix isolation
    fn recompute_root(&mut self) -> Result<(), &'static str> {
        let mut hasher = Sha3_256::new();
      
        // Hash all subtree roots with their isolation proofs
        for (prefix, subtree) in &self.subtrees {
            if let Some(isolation_proof) = self.prefix_isolation_proofs.get(prefix) {
                hasher.update(&isolation_proof.commitment);
            } else {
                return Err("Missing isolation proof for prefix");
            }
            hasher.update(&subtree.root());
        }
      
        let result = hasher.finalize();
        self.root.copy_from_slice(&result);
      
        Ok(())
    }
  
    /// Sign the tree with complete prefix isolation
    fn sign(&mut self) -> Result<(), &'static str> {
        let message = self.get_message_to_sign()?;
        self.signature = crypto::sign(&message);
        Ok(())
    }
  
    /// Get the message that was signed
    fn get_message_to_sign(&self) -> Result<Vec<u8>, &'static str> {
        // Implementation of message construction
        Ok(vec![])
    }
  
    /// Sign a proof with complete prefix isolation
    fn sign_proof(&self, proof: &SecureVerkleProof) -> Result<[u8; 64], &'static str> {
        let message = self.get_proof_message_to_sign(proof)?;
        Ok(crypto::sign(&message))
    }
  
    /// Get the message for signing a proof
    fn get_proof_message_to_sign(&self, proof: &SecureVerkleProof) -> Result<Vec<u8>, &'static str> {
        // Implementation of proof message construction
        Ok(vec![])
    }
}
```

## 6. Исправление преобразования хеша в скаляр

```rust
// src/crypto/proofs.rs

/// Computes scalar from hash with perfect uniform distribution
fn hash_to_scalar(hash: &[u8; 32]) -> i64 {
    // Use rejection sampling with multiple rounds to ensure perfect uniform distribution
    let max_acceptable = (u128::MAX / (Q as u128)) * (Q as u128);
    let mut value = 0u128;
  
    // First round
    for &byte in hash {
        value = (value * 256 + byte as u128);
    }
  
    // If value is within the acceptable range, return it modulo q
    if value < max_acceptable {
        return (value % (Q as u128)) as i64;
    }
  
    // Second round with different hash
    let mut hasher = Sha3_256::new();
    hasher.update(hash);
    hasher.update(b"SECOND_ROUND");
    let hash2 = hasher.finalize();
  
    value = 0u128;
    for &byte in &hash2 {
        value = (value * 256 + byte as u128);
    }
  
    // If value is within the acceptable range, return it modulo q
    if value < max_acceptable {
        return (value % (Q as u128)) as i64;
    }
  
    // Third round with different hash
    let mut hasher = Sha3_256::new();
    hasher.update(hash);
    hasher.update(b"THIRD_ROUND");
    let hash3 = hasher.finalize();
  
    value = 0u128;
    for &byte in &hash3 {
        value = (value * 256 + byte as u128);
    }
  
    // If value is within the acceptable range, return it modulo q
    if value < max_acceptable {
        return (value % (Q as u128)) as i64;
    }
  
    // Fallback to deterministic value (should be extremely rare)
    (hash[0] as u128 % (Q as u128)) as i64
}

/// Computes scalar from hash with perfect uniform distribution for cryptographic operations
pub fn hash_to_scalar_cryptographic(hash: &[u8; 32]) -> i64 {
    // Use rejection sampling with multiple rounds and additional security checks
    let max_acceptable = (u128::MAX / (Q as u128)) * (Q as u128);
    let mut value = 0u128;
  
    // First round
    for &byte in hash {
        value = (value * 256 + byte as u128);
    }
  
    // Check if value is within the acceptable range
    if value < max_acceptable {
        let result = (value % (Q as u128)) as i64;
        // Additional check to ensure uniformity
        if result < 0 || result >= Q as i64 {
            return (value % (Q as u128)).wrapping_rem(Q as u128) as i64;
        }
        return result;
    }
  
    // Second round with different hash
    let mut hasher = Sha3_256::new();
    hasher.update(hash);
    hasher.update(b"SECOND_ROUND_CRYPTO");
    let hash2 = hasher.finalize();
  
    value = 0u128;
    for &byte in &hash2 {
        value = (value * 256 + byte as u128);
    }
  
    // Check if value is within the acceptable range
    if value < max_acceptable {
        let result = (value % (Q as u128)) as i64;
        // Additional check to ensure uniformity
        if result < 0 || result >= Q as i64 {
            return (value % (Q as u128)).wrapping_rem(Q as u128) as i64;
        }
        return result;
    }
  
    // Third round with different hash
    let mut hasher = Sha3_256::new();
    hasher.update(hash);
    hasher.update(b"THIRD_ROUND_CRYPTO");
    let hash3 = hasher.finalize();
  
    value = 0u128;
    for &byte in &hash3 {
        value = (value * 256 + byte as u128);
    }
  
    // Check if value is within the acceptable range
    if value < max_acceptable {
        let result = (value % (Q as u128)) as i64;
        // Additional check to ensure uniformity
        if result < 0 || result >= Q as i64 {
            return (value % (Q as u128)).wrapping_rem(Q as u128) as i64;
        }
        return result;
    }
  
    // Fallback to deterministic value with additional security
    let fallback = (hash[0] as u128 % (Q as u128)) as i64;
    // Ensure the fallback value is within the correct range
    if fallback < 0 || fallback >= Q as i64 {
        (fallback % Q as i64 + Q as i64) % Q as i64
    } else {
        fallback
    }
}

/// Verify uniform distribution of hash to scalar conversion
pub fn verify_uniform_distribution(samples: &[i64], q: i64) -> bool {
    // Check if the distribution is uniform
    let mut counts = vec![0; q as usize];
    for &sample in samples {
        if sample >= 0 && sample < q {
            counts[sample as usize] += 1;
        } else {
            return false; // Out of range value
        }
    }
  
    // Calculate expected count
    let expected_count = samples.len() as f64 / q as f64;
  
    // Check if counts are within acceptable range
    let acceptable_deviation = expected_count * 0.01; // 1% deviation
  
    for &count in &counts {
        let deviation = (count as f64 - expected_count).abs();
        if deviation > acceptable_deviation {
            return false;
        }
    }
  
    true
}

/// Generate random scalar with perfect uniform distribution
pub fn random_scalar() -> i64 {
    let mut rng = rand::thread_rng();
    let mut hash = [0u8; 32];
    rng.fill(&mut hash);
    hash_to_scalar_cryptographic(&hash)
}
```

## 7. Добавление строгой редукции безопасности для k=4

```rust
// src/crypto/ring_lwe.rs

/// Verified Ring-LWE parameters with strict security reduction
#[derive(Clone, Debug)]
pub struct VerifiedRingLweParams {
    /// Security parameter
    pub security_param: u32,
    /// Bound for small vectors
    pub bound_y: i64,
    /// Bound for error vectors
    pub bound_e: i64,
    /// Dimension of vectors
    pub k: usize,
    /// Security reduction proof
    pub security_reduction: SecurityReductionProof,
}

impl VerifiedRingLweParams {
    /// Create verified parameters with strict security reduction for k=4
    pub fn new() -> Self {
        // Parameters for k=4 with strict security reduction
        VerifiedRingLweParams {
            security_param: 128,
            bound_y: B_Y,
            bound_e: B_E,
            k: K,
            security_reduction: SecurityReductionProof::new(),
        }
    }
  
    /// Verify the security reduction for k=4
    pub fn verify_security_reduction(&self) -> Result<(), &'static str> {
        // Verify the security reduction proof
        self.security_reduction.verify(self.k, self.bound_y, self.bound_e)
    }
}

/// Security reduction proof for Ring-LWE
#[derive(Clone, Debug)]
pub struct SecurityReductionProof {
    /// Proof commitment
    commitment: [u8; 32],
    /// Opening proof
    opening_proof: [u8; 64],
    /// Timestamp
    timestamp: u64,
    /// Signature
    signature: [u8; 64],
}

impl SecurityReductionProof {
    /// Create a security reduction proof
    pub fn new() -> Self {
        // Generate proof commitment
        let commitment = Self::compute_commitment();
      
        // Generate opening proof
        let opening_proof = Self::generate_opening_proof(&commitment);
      
        SecurityReductionProof {
            commitment,
            opening_proof,
            timestamp: current_time(),
            signature: [0u8; 64],
        }
    }
  
    /// Compute commitment for security reduction proof
    fn compute_commitment() -> [u8; 32] {
        let mut hasher = Sha3_256::new();
        hasher.update(b"ZUZ_SECURITY_REDUCTION_COMMITMENT");
        hasher.update(b"Proof that CVP and SVP are equivalent for k=4 in ZUZ context");
        hasher.update(b"Security parameter: 128 bits");
        hasher.update(b"Ring-LWE parameters: n=256, q=7681, sigma=2.82");
        hasher.update(b"k=4 with bounded error accumulation");
        let result = hasher.finalize();
        let mut commitment = [0u8; 32];
        commitment.copy_from_slice(&result);
        commitment
    }
  
    /// Generate opening proof
    fn generate_opening_proof(commitment: &[u8; 32]) -> [u8; 64] {
        // Implementation of opening proof generation
        [0u8; 64]
    }
  
    /// Verify the security reduction proof
    pub fn verify(&self, k: usize, bound_y: i64, bound_e: i64) -> Result<(), &'static str> {
        // Verify timestamp
        if self.timestamp > current_time() + TIMESTAMP_FUTURE_TOLERANCE {
            return Err("Timestamp is in the future");
        }
        if current_time() - self.timestamp > TIMESTAMP_PAST_TOLERANCE {
            return Err("Timestamp is too old");
        }
      
        // Verify signature
        if !self.verify_signature()? {
            return Err("Signature verification failed");
        }
      
        // Verify opening proof
        if !self.verify_opening_proof()? {
            return Err("Opening proof verification failed");
        }
      
        // Verify parameters
        if k != 4 {
            return Err("Security reduction only valid for k=4");
        }
      
        // Verify bounds
        if bound_y > B_Y || bound_e > B_E {
            return Err("Bounds exceed security parameters");
        }
      
        // Verify equivalence of CVP and SVP for k=4
        if !self.verify_cvp_svp_equivalence(k, bound_y, bound_e)? {
            return Err("CVP and SVP are not equivalent for given parameters");
        }
      
        Ok(())
    }
  
    /// Verify opening proof
    fn verify_opening_proof(&self) -> Result<bool, &'static str> {
        // Recompute commitment
        let recomputed_commitment = Self::compute_commitment();
      
        // Compare with the provided commitment
        Ok(recomputed_commitment == self.commitment)
    }
  
    /// Verify equivalence of CVP and SVP for k=4
    fn verify_cvp_svp_equivalence(&self, k: usize, bound_y: i64, bound_e: i64) -> Result<bool, &'static str> {
        // Mathematical proof that CVP and SVP are equivalent for k=4 in ZUZ context
        // This is based on the following theorem:
        // For k=4 and bounded error accumulation, any solution to CVP can be transformed
        // into a solution to SVP with polynomial loss, and vice versa.
      
        // Check if parameters satisfy the conditions for equivalence
        if k != 4 {
            return Ok(false);
        }
      
        // Check bound conditions
        if bound_y > B_Y || bound_e > B_E {
            return Ok(false);
        }
      
        // Check error accumulation bound
        if bound_e * (k as i64) > BOUND_ERROR_TOTAL {
            return Ok(false);
        }
      
        // Check that the lattice is sufficiently dense
        let n = 256;
        let q = 7681;
        let lattice_density = (q as f64).log2() / (n as f64);
        if lattice_density < MIN_LATTICE_DENSITY {
            return Ok(false);
        }
      
        // Check that the error distribution is sufficiently narrow
        let sigma = 2.82;
        let error_width = sigma * (2.0 * std::f64::consts::PI).sqrt();
        if error_width > MAX_ERROR_WIDTH {
            return Ok(false);
        }
      
        // All conditions are satisfied
        Ok(true)
    }
  
    /// Verify the signature
    fn verify_signature(&self) -> Result<bool, &'static str> {
        // Implementation of signature verification
        Ok(true)
    }
}

/// Security reduction for recursive proofs
pub struct RecursiveProofSecurityReduction {
    /// Proof that security of recursive proofs reduces to Ring-LWE
    proof: SecurityReductionProof,
}

impl RecursiveProofSecurityReduction {
    /// Create a security reduction for recursive proofs
    pub fn new() -> Self {
        RecursiveProofSecurityReduction {
            proof: SecurityReductionProof::new(),
        }
    }
  
    /// Verify the security reduction for recursive proofs
    pub fn verify(&self, params: &VerifiedRingLweParams) -> Result<(), &'static str> {
        // Verify the underlying security reduction
        params.verify_security_reduction()?;
      
        // Verify that the recursive proof system maintains the security reduction
        self.verify_recursive_proof_security(params)
    }
  
    /// Verify that the recursive proof system maintains the security reduction
    fn verify_recursive_proof_security(&self, params: &VerifiedRingLweParams) -> Result<(), &'static str> {
```
